        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552149419" href="/book/show/399415.Monstrous_Regiment">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">hardcore Discworld fans but its not for newbies</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Shovelmonkey1 by: </span>
      A life long discworld affection
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3926982-shovelmonkey1?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168847340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5777303964286312126">Normally I would include a Pratchett book on my "clear-unparalled-genius" shelf but this one is not getting a spot on there. I've read everything that Pratchett has written (Discworld, Gaimen collaborations, plus the Diggers/Truckers/Wings books and other discworld spin-offs) and while this book is clever in the trademark Pratchett way, the story is less funny because it is closer to the real world than many of the others in the series. The charm of the Discworld is that normally its like lookin</span>
  <span id="freeText5777303964286312126" style="display:none">Normally I would include a Pratchett book on my "clear-unparalled-genius" shelf but this one is not getting a spot on there. I've read everything that Pratchett has written (Discworld, Gaimen collaborations, plus the Diggers/Truckers/Wings books and other discworld spin-offs) and while this book is clever in the trademark Pratchett way, the story is less funny because it is closer to the real world than many of the others in the series. The charm of the Discworld is that normally its like looking at life through the wrong end of a telescope- the reality is further away than usual. This one does the reverse and highlights real world issues; the legality of war, equal rights, and the politics of laying down your life for religion. Difficult to make most of this stuff funny at the best of times but Pratchett does manage it in places. Still enough funnies to raise a wry smile but if you're looking for belly laughs then you need to look elsewhere on the Discworld.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5777303964286312126" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2137903" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2137903" />
    <a title="anenko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/118409-anenko"><img alt="anenko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1188780196p2/118409.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2137903?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="anenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="anenko" href="/user/show/118409-anenko">anenko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/118409-anenko?shelf=fantasy-and-paranormal">fantasy-and-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/118409-anenko?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/118409-anenko?shelf=crossdressing-and-genderfuck">crossdressing-and-genderfuck</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2137903" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6153613497538496197">It seems that every genre fan worth the name should read at least one Pratchett novel. I find the large body of works devoted to Discworld rather intimidating, which is why Monstrous Regiment is one of the few Discworld novels that I have read. With the exception of a few preexisting characters, this novel stands well on it’s own. Above and beyond that, I was drawn to this book because it is about women disguising themselves as men--and I have a weakness for stories about crossdressing heroines.</span>
  <span id="freeText6153613497538496197" style="display:none">It seems that every genre fan worth the name should read at least one Pratchett novel. I find the large body of works devoted to Discworld rather intimidating, which is why Monstrous Regiment is one of the few Discworld novels that I have read. With the exception of a few preexisting characters, this novel stands well on it’s own. Above and beyond that, I was drawn to this book because it is about women disguising themselves as men--and I have a weakness for stories about crossdressing heroines. <br /><br />Monstrous Regiment was a quick, engaging read. The humour was present throughout, but never overwhelming. There were some serious and deeply moving moments, especially when dealing with what it meant to be a woman and a soldier Borogravia, a deeply troubled country. I liked all of the characters, and the development of the squad as a team and as friends. While the ending is open-ended, I adore it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6153613497538496197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1102213459" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1102213459" />
    <a title="Priscilla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75336-priscilla"><img alt="Priscilla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447009311p2/75336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1102213459?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Priscilla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Priscilla" href="/user/show/75336-priscilla">Priscilla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75336-priscilla?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75336-priscilla?shelf=fantasy-military">fantasy-military</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1102213459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14561657572346794861">Confession time: The first time I read Monstrous Regiment, when it was released in 2003, I didn't like it. As a big fan of the City Watch, I resented that we were teased with cameos from Vimes and Angua but we didn't see their characters evolve, and I thought the ending was too contrived. From the sidelines, I watched my fellow fans EXPLODE with love for the book and produce reams of fanart and fanfic, never participating myself. I made a mental note to maybe give it another go, but I never got </span>
  <span id="freeText14561657572346794861" style="display:none">Confession time: The first time I read Monstrous Regiment, when it was released in 2003, I didn't like it. As a big fan of the City Watch, I resented that we were teased with cameos from Vimes and Angua but we didn't see their characters evolve, and I thought the ending was too contrived. From the sidelines, I watched my fellow fans EXPLODE with love for the book and produce reams of fanart and fanfic, never participating myself. I made a mental note to maybe give it another go, but I never got around to it.<br /><br />Now eleven years later, in a fit of feminist fury, I bought the audio edition and listened over the span of a few days. Oh my god, this book is phenomenal. <br /><br />I think I read it at the wrong point in my life. In 2003, I'd just graduated from an all-girls' high school. I went to an all-girls' summer camp for a big chunk of my childhood, too. I was fed a steady diet of girl power propaganda, which was ultimately meaningless because I didn't really understand what it was like to live in a universe with men in it and feel lesser or unwelcome. I grew up with Female as default, and I was told I could have anything I wanted, because I wanted to be an engineer and the world was desperate for women engineers! Of course, one month into my first semester of my 90% male computer science major, when this book came out, my ego was busy being CRUSHED. I felt like everything I'd been promised was a lie, because the subject that had always come easy to me was kicking my butt, and I had no idea how to make friends to work and study with, making me even more useless. I don't know if I resented the book because it was too close to home, or if I was in denial about what I was experiencing, but now that I've grown and rebuilt my self image, I can fully appreciate this marvel of a book and the struggles Polly faces. It wasn't what I needed at 18, but it's exactly what I needed right now.<br /><br />And more than that, I feel like the universe has given me a gift. It's like discovering a gem from Pratchett's heyday for the first time. I love these characters. I love the world they discover and how they shape it. This book is GENIUS. I actually got a little teary explaining to my roommate about how meaningful the experience of rediscovering this book was. It's like my favorite author of the time reached forward into the future to write the book I needed when he was still in prime shape to write it. Thanks, Pterry.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14561657572346794861" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="An Odd1" class="user" itemprop="url" name="An Odd1" href="/user/show/4863716-an-odd1">An Odd1</a>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781843950738" href="/book/show/8870689-monstrous-regiment">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863716-an-odd1?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer278787063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3662797525784386417">Polly "Perks" blonde Borogravian barmaid cuts her braids, practices her belching and swaggering, and joins tobacco-chewer legendary Sergeant Jack Jackrum's little lads. Perks seeks her big slow-witted brother Paul, one of the many missing In-and-out troopers. "Shufti" Manickle seeks "Dear John". <br/><br/>"Tonker" Halter keeps close to and restrains pyromaniac pal "Lofty" Tewt. Vampire Maladict is addicted to coffee instead of blood. Frail "Wazzer" Goom prays, more fervently than the average citizen, and </span>
  <span id="freeText3662797525784386417" style="display:none">Polly "Perks" blonde Borogravian barmaid cuts her braids, practices her belching and swaggering, and joins tobacco-chewer legendary Sergeant Jack Jackrum's little lads. Perks seeks her big slow-witted brother Paul, one of the many missing In-and-out troopers. "Shufti" Manickle seeks "Dear John". <br /><br />"Tonker" Halter keeps close to and restrains pyromaniac pal "Lofty" Tewt. Vampire Maladict is addicted to coffee instead of blood. Frail "Wazzer" Goom prays, more fervently than the average citizen, and even Listens to the Duchess, unseen for decades, but better than the god Nuggan who declares increasingly insane Abominations: the color blue, oysters, babies. <br /><br />Zombie Igor expertly sews on limbs, like all the Igor tribe. Huge troll Carborundum is slow, but rock hard. Their officer, Lieutenant Blouse, myopic desk jockey, creator of new filing system, is encouraged to keep his eye on the big picture and allow his commands to be anticipated. <br /><br />Meanwhile at enemy headquarters, we glimpse (from Discworld Snuff) Sam Vines, Ankh-Morpork (and allies) army chief seeking any means of truce, and spying hope in the small merry band of monsters. The final castle battle reveals astonishing secrets about the top military leaders. Humor wins us over to support female capability. "And the new day was a great big fish."<br /><br />Except for the frontspiece satirical political cartoon, most of cast are listed above. Curvy females won't identify with Polly pretending to be a boy, but I was a scrawny flat kid, and got mistaken for male even as a long-haired teen. <br /><br />The extensive eccentric cast and their interaction catch my curiosity. What will they do next? Not so fond of the name-dropping Sam Vimes cameo, and well-done plot: girl as boy grows up going to war. <br /><br />For an old guy, Pratchett is observant of the benefits of pockets in male clothing. Maybe female shoes are not so important pointed where country's economy is based on a clog.</span>

    <a title="Karla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2846441-karla"><img alt="Karla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537371209p2/2846441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/531341772?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karla" href="/user/show/2846441-karla">Karla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780060013165" href="/book/show/386371.Monstrous_Regiment">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2846441-karla?shelf=dead-tree">dead-tree</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer531341772" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9072502938728006151"><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[The "guys" are all chicks! <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It's a plot gimmick that never gets old, even after the tenth surprise reveal!<br/><br/>Haha, uh, NO.<br/><br/>I'm sure his fans would tell me this wasn't the best Pratchett to start with. My choices are always so BAD for highly-rated authors! ;D<br/><br/>His humor isn't exactly a ha-ha kind of funny. More a very quiet kind of funny. So quiet I missed it entirely.</span>
  <span id="freeText9072502938728006151" style="display:none"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The "guys" are all chicks! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It's a plot gimmick that never gets old, even after the tenth surprise reveal!<br /><br />Haha, uh, NO.<br /><br />I'm sure his fans would tell me this wasn't the best Pratchett to start with.   <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2180458624" />
    <a title="Marta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2168708-marta"><img alt="Marta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271458432p2/2168708.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2180458624?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060013158" href="/book/show/513534.Monstrous_Regiment">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2168708-marta?shelf=humor">humor</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2180458624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13475866998288965635">One of Pratchett’s best, a later work with polished writing and a sensible plot. Pratchett goes full on feminist and anti-war with this one. Great characters and observations, as usual. It is a stand-alone Discworld book, with some beloved Ankh-Morpork characters making cameos. Great fun and very relevant today.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2634280367" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2634280367" />
    <a title="Chip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1916743-chip"><img alt="Chip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444485238p2/1916743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2634280367?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chip" href="/user/show/1916743-chip">Chip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1916743-chip?shelf=discworld">discworld</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2634280367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9937455010713629422">One day.<br/><br/>That's what it took me to read this book. I've read other books in one day, but allow me to give you some context. I'm currently on a restricted diet to prepare for an upcoming screening to ensure my cancer is still in remission. This diet leads to a loss of energy and makes me sleep a lot. I picked up this book when I got out of bed on Sunday and stayed up until just after midnight reading it (to be fair, I didn't read the entire time, but I needed to complete the book before going to b</span>
  <span id="freeText9937455010713629422" style="display:none">One day.<br /><br />That's what it took me to read this book. I've read other books in one day, but allow me to give you some context. I'm currently on a restricted diet to prepare for an upcoming screening to ensure my cancer is still in remission. This diet leads to a loss of energy and makes me sleep a lot. I picked up this book when I got out of bed on Sunday and stayed up until just after midnight reading it (to be fair, I didn't read the entire time, but I needed to complete the book before going to bed). My work self yesterday was exhausted, but I have no regrets (although I did sleep about 10-11 hours Monday night).<br /><br />While <i>most</i> of the other books in the series have been enjoyable (I won't lie, there were a few that were slogs), it has been worth it for the ones that are gems. Those other books serve as great background context for books such as this.<br /><br />Characters: 5*<br />This book goes beyond the other books in this series in terms of character development. While other characters tend to evolve over an entire book, our protagonist Polly manages to grow and learn within the course of a single story. Plus, this book had the return of a few of my favorite characters from the other books in the series.<br /><br />Plot: 5*<br />This book managed to stay focused on the primary plot without a ton of side plots that sometimes detract from Discworld stories. Yes, there was a secondary plot, but it was much more of a palette cleanser and it did serve to move the primary plot forward.<br /><br />Universe: 4.95*<br />While the universe of Discworld is a vast and wondrous one and this particular story did an excellent job filling in the corners of that universe, if I had any qualms at all about this book, it was that it didn't move the needle forward in the exploration of the universe. The universe itself did impact the story line, but it was much more of a background player than in other books that I love. It didn't detract from the story at all - it just didn't really move the story forward.<br /><br />Bonus category - the ending: 5*<br />One area that I frequently am slightly annoyed by - even in the strong Discworld books - is the ending. This book ends well. No sudden endings, no loose plot threads, no confusion. It was clean and it was satisfying.<br /><br />And, as is my custom on books by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" title="Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry Pratchett</a>, here are my favorite quotes:<br />“The presence of those seeking the truth is infinitely to be preferred to the presence of those who think they've found it.” <br /><br />“Do you think it's possible for an entire nation to be insane?” <br /><br />“The enemy wasn't men, or women, or the old, or even the dead. It was just bleedin' stupid people, who came in all varieties. And no one had the right to be stupid.” <br /><br />“It's not lying when you do it to officers!” <br /><br />“Good or bad, do it as you. Too many lies and there's no truth to go back to.” <br /><br />“[The pamphlet] was very patriotic. That is, it talked about killing foreigners.” <br /><br />“Anyway, why would you trust anything written down? She certainly didn't trust "Mothers of Borogravia!" and that was from the government. And if you couldn't trust the government, who could you trust?<br />Very nearly everyone, come to think of it...” <br /><br />“...felt questing eyes boring into her. She was embarrassed, of course. But not for the obvious reason. It was for the other one, the little lesson that life sometimes rams home with a stick: you are not the only one watching the world. Other people are people; while you watch them they watch you, and they think about you while you think about them. The world isn’t just about you.” <br /><br />“I want to eat chocolates in a great big room where the world is a different place.” <br /><br />“Sooner or later all things are numbers, yes?” <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9937455010713629422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1517875324" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1517875324" />
    <a title="Jody" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23038885-jody"><img alt="Jody" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590792983p2/23038885.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1517875324?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jody" href="/user/show/23038885-jody">Jody</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23038885-jody?shelf=on-my-e-shelf">on-my-e-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23038885-jody?shelf=aty-reject-challenge">aty-reject-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23038885-jody?shelf=aty-2017">aty-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1517875324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13950710584740270657">I really enjoyed this - Terry Pratchett really just <i>got it</i>. And by "it" I mean, well, pretty much everything. Brilliant & witty, and very clever. I found it a little long though, a little too padded. I don't know if it's because I'm in a bit of a reading slump at the moment, but this took me way longer than it should have to read, mostly because I didn't feel the momentum I was looking for. I think this one will deserve a re-read down the track, when I'm back in my groove.</span>
  <span id="freeText13950710584740270657" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this - Terry Pratchett really just <i>got it</i>. And by "it" I mean, well, pretty much everything. Brilliant &amp; witty, and very clever. I found it a little long though, a little too padded. I don't know if it's because I'm in a bit of a reading slump at the moment, but this took me way longer than it should have to read, mostly because I didn't feel the momentum I was looking for. I think this one will deserve a re-read down the track, when I'm back in my groove.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Sf1kEurmlUpRKn66UoSHDhJW8vIZiYHVrndO8PVfPZRz2w3AUbhcIvYBytulcY3RxAkVOtcED7L1CQhBOBzPDg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TlrJ4WM94oyLU6U8Hr+n7ULIdpiAq33AodcqboGrprt0fKAz2GMr5Cx4EV3pSq0ylJeRUE4m86f6qWzfTOhUIQ==')})

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13331101912963594319">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br/><br/>Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, i</span>
  <span id="freeText13331101912963594319" style="display:none">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel, <i>The Color of Magic</i>, in 1983. In 1987, he turned to writing full time. <br /><br />There are over 40 books in the Discworld series, of which four are written for children. The first of these, <i>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</i>, won the Carnegie Medal. <br /><br />A non-Discworld book, <i>Good Omens</i>, his 1990 collaboration with Neil Gaiman, has been a longtime bestseller and was reissued in hardcover by William Morrow in early 2006 (it is also available as a mass market paperback - Harper Torch, 2006 - and trade paperback - Harper Paperbacks, 2006). <br /><br />In 2008, Harper Children's published Terry's standalone non-Discworld YA novel, <i>Nation</i>. Terry published <i>Snuff</i> in October 2011. <br /><br />Regarded as one of the most significant contemporary English-language satirists, Pratchett has won numerous literary awards, was named an Officer of the British Empire (OBE) “for services to literature” in 1998, and has received honorary doctorates from the University of Warwick in 1999, the University of Portsmouth in 2001, the University of Bath in 2003, the University of Bristol in 2004, Buckinghamshire New University in 2008, the University of Dublin in 2008, Bradford University in 2009, the University of Winchester in 2009, and The Open University in 2013 for his contribution to Public Service.<br /><br />In Dec. of 2007, Pratchett disclosed that he had been diagnosed with Alzheimer's disease. On 18 Feb, 2009, he was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /><br />Sir Terry Pratchett passed away on 12th March 2015.</span>
